Women's World

Reflections on the Student Unrest at Suzhou Women's Normal School

— Liu Yu

In recent years, under the impetus of "rectifying academic style" and "bearing humiliation and burden, burying oneself in studies," students across the country have long become herds of docile lambs. They either bury themselves under the window, diligently pursuing academic credits and diplomas, or they live in a drunken dream, clinging to the enjoyment before their eyes. The active spirit of the "May Fourth" and "May Thirtieth" eras has long since vanished. In such a silent atmosphere, the students of Suzhou Women's Normal School unexpectedly launched the "expulsion of the principal unrest" on May 14. This is indeed a major event worthy of attention.

According to a report by the Jiangsu Education Department on July 9, the main cause of this unrest was "due to the issue of the retention or dismissal of the Director of Moral Education, Sun Qimin, teachers interfered, and students coerced the signing of contracts"; and Sun Qimin "apparently condoned and instructed" the unrest. It is of course impossible to make a rash judgment as to whether the aforementioned reasons are true; however, simply based on the above report, we cannot help but raise our doubts. If the Director of Moral Education Sun Qimin "behaved improperly and had impure thoughts," why was she able to "instruct" the entire school's students to come forward and retain her, and even cause "overly regulated behavior" such as "coercing the signing of contracts!" On the other hand, why was Principal Chen, who supposedly "has been the principal for eight years and has achieved remarkable results," instead expelled by all the students? That is to say, students' thinking is naive and easily manipulated; but in secondary schools with "remarkable achievements," having received five or six years of education, and soon to become teachers, they should not be completely without the ability to distinguish this crucial issue!

Taking a step back, even if the cause of the unrest was indeed due to teachers' "condoning and instructing," the responsibility cannot be pushed to the students; because the hiring of teachers is entirely the principal's prerogative. It is heard that the Director of Moral Education who was dismissed this time has been teaching at the school for six years, has always been admired by the principal, and has even won a commendation from the Education Department. If it is indeed true that she "behaved improperly and had impure thoughts"; the principal should first bear the responsibility. The Education Department, on the one hand, admits that the principal "failed to properly select personnel," and on the other hand, uses the phrase "has been the principal for eight years and has achieved remarkable results" to lightly cover it up, but the so-called "remarkable achievements" have no factual proof; what we see is only such a small "achievement" as causing the expulsion of the entire school's students. From this point of view, the so-called "has been the principal for eight years and has achieved remarkable results" is as incomprehensible as "behaved improperly and had impure thoughts."

Finally, regarding the students, the end of this unrest resulted in the expulsion of as many as ten students, which was probably unexpected. But in the eyes of those with even a little social science knowledge, this is not surprising. There is no such thing as absolute right and wrong in the world; the "legitimate demands" in one position will become "overly regulated actions" in another position. Conversely, in the eyes of students, that kind of "lamb"-like education also has its social basis. If it is thought that this is the matter of a few people, and it can be resolved by the retention or dismissal of a few people: then they will inevitably receive the most severe lesson.

Women's Issues Lecture

Section 3: Free Love and Marriage

— Jun Hui

The Industrial Revolution also brought about significant changes in love and marriage relationships.

We know that in the slave economic era, there was so-called buying marriage, which is a marriage where livestock, grains, and cash are used as payment to buy a bride. Also, in the feudal era, there was so-called blind marriage, which is a marriage that is forcibly arranged regardless of the wishes of the parties involved, based solely on the interests of the family and family economy. In other words, it is all the "parental command, matchmaker's word" marriage in China. However, in capitalist society, that kind of marriage form could no longer be suitable for the social organization of capitalists, so it was abandoned and a new marriage relationship was created, which is the so-called sacred free love and marriage contract.

When the industrial and commercial citizens first appeared on the stage of history, they indeed swore the freedom of marriage, recognized the right of the parties involved in the marriage to choose their own partners, and even praised the union based on the true consent and mutual sexual love between the two sexes. However, this is only a reflection of the liberalism of civil society. In reality, so-called "free" love inevitably becomes the prisoner of money under the complex economic relationships of selfishness. In detail, in propertied society, so-called free love, no matter how pure and sincere its motivation, cannot but be restricted by monetary relations. The love affair between Huang Huiru and Lu Genrong, master and servant, which caused a sensation in Shanghai a few years ago, ultimately did not exceed that principle. Moreover, in this society dominated by the "sacred" private ownership of property, many people with ulterior motives even regard love as a speculative means to acquire property!

Propertied society replaced the previous buying and arranged marriage system with a commercial marriage contract. "The parties involved in the marriage became contractors who carried out transactions with 'equal' qualifications. These parties mutually become buyers and sellers." Among them, one party guarantees love with money, and the other party exchanges money for love. So-called marriage completely belongs to the laws of the capitalist commodity market. Capitalism "liberated" women from the buying and arranged marriage system, making them "businesswomen" who had no choice but to sell love. The modern British novelist Arnold wrote this about the heroine in his novel "Like":

"She received special training in order to get a man with property, and she finally succeeded. That is, she married the Duke of Sherrill. This is equivalent to marrying 20,000 acres of land in England, 4,000 acres of land in Scotland, a property in Piccadilly, seven properties in various towns and cities, a steam yacht, and 500,000 pounds of Central England Railway stock, etc."

This is what is said to tens of millions of men and women, young and old, in capitalist society, and it is the formula of marriage in propertied society. In other words, almost everyone has to marry the owner of a coal mine, oil, department store, etc., and has to marry the boss of bank deposits, gold and silver jewelry, steel factories, etc.

Bebel said it well about marriage in propertied society! He said: "Money marriage is the safest and easiest way to achieve high-level social life! One side desires as much money as possible, and the other side yearns for titles, honors, and status. In the upper class, they seek satisfactory objects in this way. Thus, marriage becomes a transaction, a customary union, where two people show respect, but in their hearts, each person has their own ideas."

In reality, it is not only women who pursue rich men; at the same time, men also seek women with property. That is to say, those who hope to acquire wealth and officials who are poor in campaign expenses seek daughters with money and power, hoping to obtain property at the same time as their wives. Especially after women acquired property inheritance rights, this tendency became even more obvious. What is this if not the prostitution of marriage!

Of course, under the conditions of capitalist society, when women without economic independence must live a life of eternal parasitism on their fathers or husbands, this prostitution is unavoidable. Regarding this point, we can see very clear evidence among working women. A worker's daughter gains economic independence very early. At the same time, she gains independence from her family. This kind of woman decides her own destiny by her own strength and solves marriage problems according to her own personal will.

When a woman can live entirely by her own strength, her love feelings will not be stained by financial considerations, and will be expressed in a very natural and pure form. The economic independence of women and its valuable influence on her love cannot be denied by even sociologists in the ruling class. Erneste, the author of "The Breakdown of the Family", Moller explains the marital relationship of working women as follows.

"If women can obtain the living resources and a certain social status that they previously obtained by marriage through their own labor, then the efforts of women to guarantee their own lives through marriage have only a small meaning. Because, except for those directly related to sexual life, almost all of her wishes are not only satisfied in marriage, but also can be satisfied outside of marriage. Therefore, she regards marriage as the realization of love and passion." (See Sociology of Family and Marriage)

Finally, here, we must understand that women with money and working women have completely different attitudes and practices towards love and marriage!

Examination and Answers on Women's Issues

— Wang Xiaoying

My letters unexpectedly attracted the attention of so many people in society, who earnestly explored various aspects of the women's movement. This proves that the women's movement has practical significance and a mission in the current stage of society. Besides expressing my utmost respect and gratitude to the gentlemen who participated in the discussion, I also feel it is necessary to say a few more words.

The "Women's Corner" has published seventy-two issues. The content is for objective facts to judge. However, since the March 8th Women's Day this year, we must admit that this exploration is its most valuable achievement. This achievement, in the process of the women's movement, is indeed worthy of attention and deep thought. The motivation for writing that letter was to correct Mr. Shiyin's points: "Why does the women's movement have to be a separate term? As if it has independent business to do," and "Women's movement, using the word 'rights' to incite people to fight." Indeed, no one can deny that women's issues are closely related to social issues. In other words, women's issues cannot be resolved independently of the entire social issue. In the summer of the year before last, the Shanghai Eight Immortals Bridge Youth Association held a lecture on social issues, and I was one of the speakers. The topic I spoke on was: "Social Issues and Women's Issues." At that time, I elaborated on the significance of this topic in detail. I never narrowly separated the women's movement from the entire social issue and targeted men as its sole target. In short, I believe that women's issues contain many complex social issues.

Now I want to give a brief answer to the articles published by Mr. Luo Qiong, Mr. Lin Gengbai, Mr. Xu Zexiang, ... - in fact, most of it is self-declaration:

(1) Regarding Mr. Luo Qiong's article published in the 70th issue of "Women's Corner," "A Review of the Chinese Women's Movement, and a Discussion on Mr. Wang Xiaoying's Letter to the Editor of Women's Youth," many of the meaningful theories mentioned in it are what I have said in the past, especially during the lecture on "Social Issues and Women's Issues" at the Youth Association in the summer of the year before last, when this meaning was discussed in detail. This time, it was only to correct Mr. Shiyin's two misunderstandings, so it was not mentioned. Now that Mr. Luo has made a special supplementary explanation, I thank him for his kindness with the greatest enthusiasm.

(2) Regarding Mr. Lin's article published in the 71st issue of "Women's Corner," "A Criticism That Is Not Criticism," it says: "The mission of the women's movement is not to make the struggle between the sexes the ultimate goal. The modern women's movement should have its important significance and should target the entire social system." In today's semi-colonial Chinese society, which is invaded by capitalism externally and suppressed by feudal ideology internally, in such an abnormal and contradictory dynamic, it is indeed not only the issue of the women's movement, but also all other issues. If you want to get a solution or improvement, you must not focus on the plane of a certain issue and ignore the three-dimensional aspects that can achieve its actual effect. Because local movements are not the most appropriate way to fundamentally solve the problem. The so-called "treat the head when it hurts, and treat the foot when it hurts" method is no longer applicable today. Mr. Lin's general meaning is quite similar to that of Mr. Luo: that women's issues cannot be resolved independently of the entire social issue. I fully agree with this point of view. As for Mr. Lin saying that I am a woman who is relatively close to the government, and I can still retain the courage of the May Fourth era to resist the recent revival movement of women, it is amazing! In fact, people in the atmosphere of the women's movement should have this consistent spirit and attitude, and should never promote the name of the women's movement for their own happiness. We must not only expose the conspiracies of those women's movement people who hang sheep's heads and sell dog meat, but also further attack them and expose their ugliness! Some people say that the result of my participation in the women's movement for more than ten years is just that I have achieved personal success; but is that really the case? No, definitely not. People who say such things may have misunderstood my personality, or mistaken the nature of things. At least I dare to say that since I have been practicing the women's movement, I have never sold my soul and conscience, and I have always taken the entire society and women as the premise, so-called "sacrificing the small self and fulfilling my duty."

(3) Regarding Mr. Xu's "Contradictions of the Women's Movement" published in the Morning Post's Sunday Review on June 9, what he said can be said to be completely aimed at modern fashionable women. He lamented the fashionable women: "... since they have unloaded all their responsibilities to the family and society, and pursue a highly Westernized life with a completely unproductive body, they go out dressed in heavy makeup, singing and dancing, and when they return, they order around, with servants and maids in front of them, and they do not hesitate to pay for the crystallization of the blood and sweat of thousands of workers and peasants as the price of rouge and perfume..." However, this can only be said to be a unique form of urban, especially Shanghai, wives, young ladies, and young mistresses. It should be known that the vast majority of women in China are still struggling and fighting under the oppression of the social class. These oppressed women, their daily lives are "hard-working and thrifty," they absolutely have not unloaded their responsibilities to the family and society, and they have not been infected with the bad habits of modern fashionable women! Mr. Xu now uses a special image to erase the general facts of women. Obviously, his focus on women is limited to a certain point of view in society, and he has failed to accurately see the state of women in the entire society, so that he only sees a small number of extravagant and wasteful modern fashionable women in modern China, and ignores the vast majority of hardworking, simple, and sincere non-fashionable women. In this wave of shouting "women go back to the family"! "Virtuous wife and good mother"! Should we still stop eating because of this? However, Mr. Xu's benevolent intentions are worthy of attention. At least his lament can give modern women who are only engaged in consumption and cannot produce a powerful warning!

As for Mr. Gao Hong's article "After Reading the Letter to the Editor of Women's Youth, Shiyin," perhaps it was because his views on the facts were different, so his remarks were also different. Although there are some points in the seven items that are worthy of acceptance, subjective prejudice is also inevitable. This is just as the editor of "Women's Corner" said: "The benevolent see benevolence, and the wise see wisdom." Due to space limitations, I will not say more here.

Finally, I hope that those who are engaged in the women's movement will pay attention to practical work, with a spirit of fearlessness and strong perseverance. Stand in the center of solving the entire social issue and seek the liberation of women at the current stage!

Mid-length Creation

Returning Home

— Su Hong

(1)

Xiuzhen left the countryside for the city three years ago. Now she has just returned from the city, and the countryside that she hasn't seen for several years is re-emerging in front of her: the mountains are still standing as before; the river is still lying meandering as before; the fields are also as before, and the path she is walking on at the moment is also stretching out as before. But she always feels a different feeling from before, she deeply feels desolate, and a kind of uneasy pressure is threatening her. Looking around carefully, everything has changed after all: on the mountain, there are no lush trees as before; the river water is not as deep as before; in the fields, there are no wheat and bean seedlings as before; on the side of the path, many mud blocks have collapsed; some of the stone slabs are also broken and crooked. She staggered along, looking into the distance at a woman washing rice at the river pier, not knowing whether it was a neighbor or an aunt, but as she approached the river pier, she saw from all the actions that the woman was her sister-in-law, but indeed she had changed like the scenery. Before, her sister-in-law was fat, with flesh all over her body, a long and round face, and red cheeks. Now she has become thin, and she doesn't know who pinched the flesh on her cheeks. The bone of her nose is high, and it is pointed and exposed.

Xiuzhen took a step forward and called out. The sister-in-law, who was busy washing rice, was stimulated by this call, and the sound that had been unfamiliar for several years suddenly appeared behind her. She suddenly raised her head, and the rice basket was almost overturned. She stared at Xiuzhen, thinking it was a stranger. Naturally, Xiuzhen has also changed now. She used to see a lively young girl, but now she is thin, yellow, and lackluster, like a dried melon. The sister-in-law was stunned for a while before she remembered:

Oh... it's sister! Oh my, you're back! Mother-in-law is really worried about you! She quickly packed up the things she had washed and walked shoulder to shoulder with Xiuzhen, and then continued, but her voice was slightly lower:

--Have you seen your brother?

--Ha! Is my brother in Shanghai? But I didn't see him. When did he go?

--It's been more than a year, and there's been no news since he left. He hasn't even sent a letter back. The sister-in-law's eyes were a little teary.

The sister-in-law walked silently closer to home. Chickens were walking in the porch, and chicken manure was all over the ground. The yellow dog barked wildly. The young mistress Wang next door was making silver ingots with the maid Ajú. Hearing the dog barking wildly, the young mistress Wang said repeatedly:

--It must be a beggar, Ajú! Close the door quickly! --There was a loud bang of closing the door

Xiuzhen's mother was sitting in front of her door chanting Buddha. Perhaps feeling that the six words "Namo Amitabha Buddha" were too troublesome to chant, she often simply chanted: Buddha, Buddha, Amitabha Buddha. She heard the dog barking at this moment, and in order to interject a few words, she chanted even more simply:

--Buddha, Buddha, Buddha,... the dog is barking again, it must be a beggar. There are really many beggars these years. Buddha, Buddha, Amitabha Buddha....

Xiuzhen saw her mother. Her mother's square face and broad body were still the same as before, but obviously she was much older. First, her eyes were much dimmer, and it seemed that one of them had become blind.

--Mom! Xiuzhen called.

--Ah! Who is it?... My Xiuzhen? The mother hurriedly stood up, and the rosary followed her. "Amitabha, my flesh, you're back!"

The mother was so happy that she was crying, she didn't know what to say, she just moved her lips tremblingly. But she was sad and loved her. She looked at her daughter's yellow and thin face, thin clothes, and a wave of sadness added to it. She knew that her daughter had returned in such a scene, with a lost appearance and empty hands, obviously she was not successful in Shanghai. She immediately led her daughter into the room, lifted her left eyelid so that she could see more clearly:

--Oh! To be so thin! She hurriedly wrapped the rosary and put it in the drawer, and then took out a piece of dried tofu. "You eat this piece of dried tofu. A few days ago, I chanted Buddha at the young mistress Wang's house, and she gave me the dried tofu as a snack. Now, everything is getting smaller. In the past, the snack for chanting Buddha was always a whole..."

Xiuzhen really didn't want to eat this moldy dried tofu, she wanted to eat something good, but she took it. She knew that she couldn't chew out any good taste from this thing, but this was a gift from her mother, a rare reunion after a long separation, and she was indeed a little hungry, so she stuffed it into her mouth, no matter how strong the cockroach smell was, she chewed it slowly, almost vomiting. The mother continued to grope, she wanted to find something else for her "treasure" - her daughter who was like a hungry louse. (To be continued)

— Wen

Shenbao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Amateur Rambling

A Fair Discussion on the Problem of Vagrant Children Relief

— Liu Xin

Since this year was designated as Children's Year from August 1, the news has spread, and people in society have paid considerable attention to children's welfare, which is one of the gratifying phenomena recently. At the same time, the public's attention is not only focused on how to educate the children of wealthy families, but also on how to relieve the poor and vagrant children, which is especially forward-looking.

On July 7, an article by Mr. Wang Maohe, "Relief for Wandering Children," was published in the Morning Post's Sunday Review, advocating the implementation of a poor children's annuity system as the only way to universally relieve vagrant children. The next day, an article by Mr. Fú, "Discussion on the Problem of Vagrant Children Relief," was published, analyzing the advantages and disadvantages of the factory system and the poor children's annuity system from an objective standpoint. The writing was fluent and incisive, and it was truly a cannon roar before the opening ceremony of Children's Year.

Searching for the articles by Mr. Wang Maohe and Mr. Fú, there is no doubt that vagrant children need relief. The focus of the debate is nothing more than the method of relieving vagrant children. Mr. Maohe believes that the poor children's annuity system is beneficial for three reasons: "(1) Giving annuities to poor children allows them to receive assistance in their families without having to enter prison-like factories; (2) Changing factory assistance to annuity assistance can save on expenses such as salaries, and children will receive more benefits; (3) A family consignment system can be implemented, with annuities paid to entrusted families to educate orphans who have no home. In the future, when orphans grow up and become adults, they will surely receive assistance from the entrusted families and become established." There are three things that can be discussed here: one, the question of whether the family consignment system is possible; two, the question of whether annuity assistance is more economical than the factory system; three, the question of whether the family consignment system is more reasonable than the factory system. Let me express my humble opinion as follows:

(1) Poor children and vagrant children are always two different kinds of categories in terms of reason: poor children are unable to live and unable to be educated because of poverty. Although they may eventually become vagrant children, they have not yet reached the point of becoming vagrant children. They have not yet acquired the wandering habits that vagrant children generally acquire. If they are rescued in time, they can live and be educated, and the method must be no different from ordinary children. Therefore, it is not impossible to adopt an annuity assistance system to relieve poor children (if fundamentally speaking, if only a certain poor family is relieved of a certain (2) child, and the other people in this certain family still cannot survive, then it is still doubtful whether this annuity assistance can be fully used to relieve this certain child, but here we are talking about dragons and tigers, so we will not go into further involvement to avoid expanding the problem), as for vagrant children, they are either orphans without parents, or poor children from proletarian peasant families, or children who have fallen on the streets without families because they have acquired bad habits or hobbies (such as stealing and smoking). They are not only poor, but also have no home. They are not only wandering, but also have bad habits. Knowing this, then we can go on to talk about how to relieve them.

Mr. Maohe, who advocates the family consignment system, wants to apply it to both poor children and vagrant children, which is really a view that is not in line with the facts. For example, China has always emphasized the concept of clan, and childless parents often adopt poor children as adopted sons. Although this does not live up to the name of "family consignment," in fact, this is also the same as the meaning of poor children's consignment. However, what childless parents want to adopt is poor children, that is, the object willing to be entrusted is poor children. As for the vagrant children walking on the streets, they are often unwilling to be adopted by childless parents. May I ask if childless parents are unwilling to adopt vagrant children with bad habits, then who else is willing to raise a wandering child and let them be with their own children?--This is a question of the possibility of facts, not a question of theory, this is a question of China, not a question of empty talk of imitation. In this way, it can be seen that the "possibility" of adopting a family consignment system to relieve vagrant children is very weak.

(2) Secondly, is annuity assistance more "economical" than the factory system? How the source of annuity assistance funds is, let's put it aside for the time being, but decentralized assistance will inevitably lead to decentralized loans. As a result, I am afraid that it can only support poor children, and at most it can only do the step of educating poor children, which can be said to be purely consumption. As for the expenses of setting up factories, it seems roughly the same as the annuity assistance funds, which is also consumption, and as the Morning Post reporter said, there is also the consumption of "employees who are not paid," but this is only a short-sighted view. Although the annuity assistance system may have investigators and supervisors who are willing to fulfill their obligations, the education is scattered and not concentrated; if the factory system, although there is a small number of employees who pay wages, a certain plan can be implemented, such as the relief of vagrant children in Soviet Russia after the revolution, which also forcibly captured all vagrant children and put them into factories. At first, it was inevitably difficult to obey and the management was quite difficult, but with gradual steps and gradual training, this group of small vagrants on the streets could actually work and produce (because they are not low-energy, but not educated), and later became good workers in factories and good construction talents in the country, which is a good lesson. We should not only regard the relief of vagrant children as a consumption action, but we should concentrate many unused labor forces and use them for production and construction. Because annuity assistance is purely consumption, while the factory system is production - although it may not be able to achieve factory self-sufficiency, it will not be more wasteful than annuity assistance - so annuity assistance is really not more economical than the factory system.

(3) Assuming that we admit that the family consignment system has the possibility of general circulation, but may I ask what kind of families are the majority of Chinese families? Most parents do not know what education is, let alone what is reasonable education. How many vigorous and promising small citizens of China are killed by the hands of these ignorant parents, and wiped out under the stupidity of not understanding reasonable education methods! If we entrust the vagrant children to families who do not understand the reasonable methods of educating children, it is no different from "asking the way to the blind"! In this way, relieving vagrant children is still just adding a mask to the face of killing vagrant children. Assuming that we believe what the Morning Post reporter said: the United States vigorously implements the family consignment system and those who are entrusted can accept the entrustment, and Chinese families will definitely be able to accept the entrustment like the United States, but what is the use of being willing to accept the entrustment but not being able to reasonably educate?

Furthermore, can these generally forced entrusted families sincerely and conscientiously be responsible for rescuing the entrusted vagrant children? I am afraid this is not necessarily the case? Although there are supervisors who fulfill their obligations and are responsible for checking there, why is it necessary to use vagrant children as a touchstone for responsibility? In this comparison, it can be seen that it is easy to ask a small number of factory employees to be responsible, but it is more difficult to ask all the entrusted families to be responsible.

Therefore, the family consignment system is far inferior to the factory system in terms of reasonable education.

In summary, the possibility of adopting a family consignment system to relieve vagrant children is very weak, the annuity assistance system is not more economical than the factory system, and the family consignment system is even far inferior to the factory system in terms of reasonable education. Although Mr. Maohe wants to take a shortcut and seek cheap, but the facts often run counter to the ideal.

Folk tale

Dragon Pearl

— Ms. Wu Ling

The sun woke up from its sleep, slowly peeking its head out from the sea. Its blood-red light immediately illuminated the earth, and it gradually rode on a red fast horse, flying straight towards the sky. The radiating light pierced through the jade-green, calm sea, penetrating the dense forest like ten thousand sharp needles, shining upon the majestic high mountains, and reaching a row of simple, old thatched huts at the foot of the mountains.

Light awakened everything: a gentle breeze blew, the green leaves of the trees swayed back and forth; birds poked their heads out of their nests, saw the smiling face of the sun, and busily called their companions to sing songs; the wildflowers on the

Page 22

meadow also straightened their waists, delicately emitting a light fragrance.

The door of a thatched hut creaked open, and a woman walked out. She went to the side of the hut and opened the door of the chicken coop. A small chick came out, clucking, and ate the millet scattered by the woman.

"Ming'er! Get up, it's not early," the woman called.

"I'm up, Mom!" Ming'er, a fifteen or sixteen-year-old, replied.

Having lost her husband early, she worked hard to raise Ming'er. She lived by spinning yarn, weaving cloth, or sewing clothes for others every day. When Ming'er grew to be eight or nine years old, he began to gather grass on the mountain, bringing it back to the market to sell after eating lunch every day, and exchanging it for some rice in the evening. In winter, he would cut trees and chop wood on the mountain, selling bundles to wealthy families. The mother and son helped each other and lived happily.

As usual, they got up very early. After eating, Ming'er took a sickle and rope and went to work on the mountain, while his mother began to weave cloth.

Saying goodbye to his mother, Ming'er walked along, singing mountain songs. He often stopped to listen to the melodious singing of the birds or bent down to pick a beautiful wildflower. Sometimes, when he encountered a strange bird or insect, he would catch it and carefully observe it. Passing through the forest, crossing the small river, a magnificent high mountain now stood before him. The mountain was covered with a layer of jade-like green grass. Stepping on it felt soft and fluffy. Skillfully climbing up, his strong body accompanied by cheerful steps, he reached the top of the mountain in a short while. Some of the grass on the mountain had already been cut and hadn't grown back, while some was still short, spread on the ground. He finally found a patch of grassland that was more than a foot tall. Overjoyed, he quickly began to work. Although he had a small body, he was strong and agile. In less than a quarter of an hour, a large area beside him was cleared. The sunlight secretly watched him through the gaps, the birds sang songs praising him, and the wind gently kissed him.

The next day, he went to the mountain as usual. When he unintentionally walked to the patch of grass he had cut the day before, he immediately discovered an astonishing phenomenon. Unexpectedly, in just one night, green grass more than a foot tall had grown back, while other places remained unchanged. He happily cut the grass, and before noon, he had already gathered as much as he could carry, so he went home. Seeing that it was still early, he went straight to the market.

His mother was washing rice by the river. From afar, she saw Ming'er coming. She was very surprised that he didn't have a basket on his back, but upon closer inspection, she saw that he was holding a paper bag in his hand. That was the rice that Ming'er usually didn't bring back until evening. How happy the mother was!

For several days in a row, he went to that patch of grass, and new grass grew out every day. He sold the grass very early every day, exchanged it for rice, and in the afternoon, he went to the mountain to cut grass, and then sold it again.

Curiosity drove him. When he went to that patch of grass today, he thought, "There must be some reason for this." So he began to look around for strange things, but there were none! Maybe the old tree next to it had a spirit, he ran over to take a look, but there was nothing. He looked east, he looked west, and busied himself for a while, but in the end, he still couldn't figure it out!

The next day, he thought that maybe there was something in the grassland, so he took a shovel with him. After cutting the grass, he dug down into the ground with the shovel, digging deeper and deeper, but there was nothing. His curiosity and determination made him continue to dig, and finally, he discovered something hard. He picked it up and looked at it. It turned out to be a small pearl, emitting a sparkling light, very beautiful. When he got home, he told his mother that it must be something precious, but his mother said that it was just a pretty pearl, and that it wasn't anything of real value! After eating dinner, it was already dark, which was when the villagers went to bed because they couldn't afford lamps. The mother and son were very surprised why it wasn't dark yet at this time, and the house was as bright as if the sun were shining. Ming'er went outside to take a look and saw the sky full of stars hanging in the sky. How strange that was! They finally discovered that the reason was that the pearl on the table was emitting light and illuminating everything.

A treasure! The mother knew it was a treasure. They were afraid that the villagers would find out, so they began to look for a place to hide it. No matter where they put it, as long as there was a small hole, its light would still shine out. Ming'er took out his clothes and wrapped it, but it didn't work. The light still shone through. Finally, they put it in the rice container, which only had a little rice left, and closed the lid. Only then did they feel relieved and happily go to sleep.

In the morning, the mother got up to prepare to cook rice. As soon as she opened the lid of the rice container, many grains of rice rolled out with a "whoosh," filling a large container full of white rice that could no longer hold any more! Amazement and joy filled the mother's heart as she shouted to wake Ming'er, tears of happiness streaming down her face!

"Ming'er! This is a good treasure, don't tell anyone else!"

But Ming'er was just a child after all, and was naturally straightforward and honest. It wasn't long before he told others. So it spread from one to ten, and from ten to a hundred, and the whole village knew!

"Ming'er, what does your treasure look like?"

"Show it to us!"

From then on, many people came to surround him every day.

Finally, because he couldn't resist them, he finally took out the pearl for them to see!

"Wow! How bright!"

"It's really a treasure!"

"I wish it were mine!"

Everyone squeezed over, pushing and shoving, crowding around Ming'er in the center, making it hard for him to breathe. Gradually, it became a disturbance. Many with malicious intentions even wanted to snatch his pearl. He quickly ran away, and many people chased after him. Finally, they caught up with him. In his anxiety, he put the pearl in his mouth and swallowed it.

The people dispersed!

Helpless, he returned home. His mother complained to him, but he didn't respond. After a while, he felt very thirsty. His mother gave him a bowl of water, and he swallowed it hungrily. However, he was still terribly thirsty, so he went to the water tank to drink, and soon he finished it! Unable to think of a solution, he had to take a bucket himself to draw water from the river. When he got to the river, he drew water into the bucket, and drank it all on the way back. Finally, he lay on the riverbank and drank, drinking endlessly. Gradually, he seemed to feel a pain in his head. He touched it and was shocked. Two horns had grown on his head. He looked into the river and saw that it was no longer his original face. He began to understand what had happened to him, and his heart filled with sorrow, but he still couldn't help but drink. Finally, his clothes fell off, and scales grew all over his body. He wanted to cry, but he couldn't. He thought of his dear mother, he wanted to shout loudly, but the sound wouldn't come out!

The sun slowly set in the west, heavily as if it already knew that this tragic scene was coming, the birds' songs also changed to a desolate tone, and the angry wind began to howl.

His mother hadn't seen Ming'er return for a long time, so she went outside to look for him. When she reached the riverbank, she saw only his clothes piled on the shore. Ming'er had already turned into a small dragon in the water, nodding to her.

"Ming'er! My Ming'er!" the mother cried and shouted, but what was the use?

The small dragon gradually grew larger, reluctantly shedding tears, always looking at his mother and nodding, unable to control himself as he swam down the river. Every time he turned his head to look at his mother, a huge wave would rise. He sadly looked at his mother twenty-four times, raising twenty-four large waves, and then gradually disappeared from sight!

The mother seemed to feel everything around her spinning and turning upside down. A wave of dizziness washed over her, and she fell down.

Industry Survey

The Ramie Cloth Industry in Sichuan

— Jia

Ramie cloth - a type of hemp fabric, called "ma bu" (hemp cloth) in Sichuan.

Sichuan ramie cloth is pure white in color, and does not "turn yellow" even when old, so the quantity sold is much larger than that produced in other provinces, and the value is also more expensive. In addition to Yunnan, Guizhou, Shanghai, Hankou and other places within the country, Korea is also a major market for its sales.

There are several counties in Sichuan that produce ramie cloth, such as Jiangjin, Longchang, Rongchang, Anle, and Lezhi, but Anle has the largest output, and Longchang ramie cloth is the most famous. This is partly because the quality produced in Longchang itself is better, and partly because Longchang is the main place where ramie cloth is shipped out of Sichuan. Therefore, when it comes to Sichuan ramie cloth, Longchang is always the representative, and even the sales signs say "Longchang."

The use of ramie cloth can be divided into two types: (1) clothing material and (2) mosquito nets. The former is more refined and the manufacturing process is very complicated, so the value is more than ten times higher than that of ramie cloth for mosquito nets. At the same time, not only is there a difference in value between the two, but each type can also be divided into seven or eight grades. Taking ramie cloth for clothing as an example: the highest grade can be sold for more than fifty yuan per bolt (each bolt can sew about two men's long gowns), and the lowest grade is about three or four yuan. As for ramie cloth for mosquito nets, each bolt is forty-eight feet long, and the price ranges from more than thirty yuan to more than two yuan. This is naturally based on the current market price in Shanghai, and sometimes the market price changes with different sales channels.

Because Longchang's ramie cloth has more sales markets, major cities in the south such as Shanghai, Guangzhou, Hankou, Hong Kong, Kunming, and Guiyang all have wholesale outlets. The opening season is always after late spring and continues until mid-autumn. Because new ramie cloth just comes on the market after late spring, and when it cools down in autumn, ramie cloth loses its function and significance.

Sichuan ramie cloth merchants who set up outlets in Shanghai are called the "Longchang Gang." They do about a million yuan of business every year. The people who manage the outlets are called "zhuang ke," and they represent local stores in Shanghai to sell goods! Ramie cloth is sent by mail from Sichuan. The "zhuang ke" receive the goods and wholesale them to other "zhuang ke." However, there is little direct contact between sellers and buyers. All are mediated by "hang ke," and all money handling is also done by "hang ke."

In previous years, ramie cloth sold very well because many people from Korea came to Shanghai to transport it, so the Sichuan ramie cloth merchants (the so-called "Longchang Gang") were all doing very well. However, in the past two or three years, sales have gradually stagnated, and the value has gradually declined. Especially this year, the market is even more tired. It is currently the hot summer season, and in theory, ramie cloth should be in high demand, but the market price still cannot rise, and it is difficult to sell even at cost. The so-called "Longchang Gang" are mostly sitting in their stores, sighing. When they see their business losing money and there is no way to save it!

The ramie cloth shipped from Sichuan to Shanghai is all mosquito net material, because mosquito nets are essential in tropical and temperate regions, and mosquito nets made of ramie cloth allow better air circulation, so sales are higher. As for clothing material, partly because the cost is too high, and partly because few people outside wear ramie cloth, most merchants do not dare to purchase this item. In the past, a bolt of ramie cloth for mosquito nets could earn a quarter of the profit after all costs, but now it is actually losing money! When the market is depressed and all industries are declining, where will the ramie cloth industry go if it doesn't follow the trend?

The raw material of ramie cloth is called ramie (zhu ma), which can be harvested three times a year! Spring, summer, and autumn. The families who grow ramie take the ramie stalks home, and the women and children strip the stalks, soak the skins in clear water tanks, and after a certain period of time, they take them out of the water to air dry. Then, they pull them into ramie fibers, and then the ramie fibers are pulled into ramie threads. These threads are purchased by weaving families or factories, woven into large batches of cloth, and then the ramie cloth merchants collect these cloths and transport them for sale in various places. There are many shops in Longchang that buy ramie cloth. According to a survey, there are roughly 30,000 yuan in transactions every day. In such a small city, such a large-scale business can be considered a unique phenomenon—

The skin of ramie is originally green, but after it is pulled into ramie thread, it appears slightly yellow because it has been soaked in water and air-dried. Therefore, after the cloth is woven, it must go through a complicated "bleaching" process: every morning before the sun rises, the ramie cloth is spread out on the lawn to absorb dew, and after the sun comes out and dries it, clean river water is sprinkled on it again. This is "processed in the same way" every day to gradually whiten the color of the cloth. After half a month, it becomes shiny and beautiful ramie cloth.

Page 23

However, this is for mosquito net ramie cloth. If it is for clothing, it is even more troublesome: when pulling ramie, fine workmanship is required to twist it into strong and delicate ramie threads. Naturally, there should be more warps when weaving, and the warps should be even, so that it is "not leaking" and "not showing stems". Only then can it be called top-grade ramie cloth. At the same time, after the cloth is woven, it must be transported to the river in Rongchang to soak. Because ramie cloth is particularly white after being eroded by the water in the Rongchang River, ramie cloth from nearby counties must be transported there to be polished. Every summer, this river is particularly lively, and this is how ramie cloth merchants are improving production.

The value of top-grade ramie cloth is several times higher than that of silk, partly because the texture of the cloth itself is better than silk, and also because it has undergone a complicated process. We often see others wearing a ramie cloth shirt and think it is ordinary, but little do we know that it is the result of the combined efforts of many people!

Scientific Miscellany

Humanity's Achievements in Conquering the Earth

— Yu Min

Discovering and conquering the Earth we live on is not an easy task, as it has many natural obstacles and difficulties that prevent humanity from understanding it. The most obvious of these difficulties are, of course, the excessively vast area of ​​the oceans, which are difficult to fly across; the obstruction of high mountains and deserts inside the mainland; and the limitation of excessively harsh climates, etc. Although humanity has now overcome the first two obvious difficulties in its hundreds of thousands of years of effort, the latter difficulty has not yet been completely overcome. Therefore, explorers of the polar regions are still working hard there, risking their lives. These natural difficulties and obstacles can only be overcome with the development of scientific technologies that can fully utilize the laws of nature, so this depends on the progress of human production methods and technology. And looking at the process of human discovery and conquest of the Earth, it is also adapted to production technology, and is by no means simply the result of curiosity and adventurousness. Without the progress of shipbuilding, you would not be able to fly across the ocean no matter how adventurous and curious you were, and the discovery of the new continent of America would have been impossible.

In terms of the separate existence of human beings on Earth, of course, human discovery of the Earth's regions has been known for a long time. However, if we are to talk about the discovery and conquest of the entire Earth by the residents of a certain region, then this achievement must be attributed to Europeans. Therefore, in terms of the overall process of understanding the Earth, it is proper to take the breadth of the scope of the discovery and conquest of it by Europeans as the process of the development of human geographical knowledge of the Earth.

Primitive people all believed that the land on Earth was a flat surface with edges. If you reached its edge, you would fall and not know where you died. Therefore, no one dared to try to explore the vastness of the Earth, and they all only wandered around the regions where they lived. If we take the Western nations as the center and talk about the discovery and conquest of the Earth, then among the most ancient nations, the first to be mentioned is the Phoenicians, for whom there is reliable evidence to know how large the area of ​​the land they discovered was. Of course, as far as the distribution of world races is concerned, it is said that the Chinese also came from the West, and even the American aborigines migrated there before the Bering Strait was formed, but this is only a primitive anthropological speculation, and not something that can be known based on the records of human cultural history. Although the Phoenicians lived in the extreme east of the Mediterranean, they had conquered lands in southern Europe, northern Africa, and the Iberian Peninsula. Of course, they would have been active in places like northern Egypt and the Babylonian region. At that time, the world they knew was only that big. The next was the Greek era. The Greeks not only knew everything that the Phoenicians knew, but they also reached the Balkans in the north, the source of the Nile in Africa, and even the Sahara. They also occasionally explored the edge of the Black Sea and the Russian Plain. The famous Alexander marched as far as Persia and India, and knew the borders of Turkestan and Guangdong, China. This was a greater expansion of the land discovered by the Phoenicians. The regions known by the early Romans naturally included everything known by the Greeks. And they also conquered Britain, expanding to the westernmost part of Europe. In Africa, they occupied places like present-day Morocco. It is said that the Romans at this time already had contact with China, and thus even knew a part of East Asia. If we want to summarize, then we can take the area conceived by Ptolemy as the area discovered by the ancient European nations, as the representative of the breadth of the world they knew at that time. He took the Mediterranean as the center, westward to the island of Great Britain, northwest to the Scandinavian Peninsula, north to the Russian Plain, east to the borders of India and southern China, and south to the upper Nile and Sudan. But on the ocean, it only reached the coasts of the Atlantic and Indian Oceans.

In the Middle Ages, Westerners, with the brave exploration of the Western Ocean by sailors from Scandinavia in the north, already knew about Iceland and Greenland, and even reached the eastern edge of Canada or the United States. This was the first time they had crossed the Atlantic Ocean. In the south, the Muslim Arabs, in order to spread the teachings of Muhammad, crossed the interior of Africa and advanced to the islands of the extreme southeast. To the west, they advanced to Europe and clashed with the Crusaders. At this time, Marco Polo, a citizen of Venice, had been to China. Through this, he knew about Japan, and on his way back, he passed through Singapore. In this way, the world known by humans in the Middle Ages can be said to have reached Greenland in the northwest, and even the border between Canada and the United States in America, reaching as far as the middle of Africa in the south, and reaching Japan and Singapore in the east.

Since the Renaissance, the theory that the Earth is spherical has been confirmed, and the enthusiasm for discovering new continents and new routes, stimulated by the demands of commerce and colonies, has become even more developed. In 1486, the Portuguese Diaz sailed to the Cape of Good Hope, and then crossed Africa by sea to India. The approximate outline of Africa was then fully known. In 1492, Columbus crossed the Atlantic and discovered the new continent of America. In 1519, the Portuguese Magellan began his circumnavigation of the world, traveling west from Europe to America, then around the southern tip of South America, across the Magellan Strait to the Pacific Ocean, and discovered the Philippines. Although Magellan died at the hands of the local aborigines, his companions completed his world voyage in 1522. In the 17th century, not only was the interior of North and South America continuously discovered, but most of it was also occupied by the Portuguese and Spanish. Summing up the Renaissance era, the known area of ​​the Earth was more than three times larger than before.

Since the 17th century, European countries have been restrained by revolutionary trends and wars. At this time, only the Netherlands continued its exploration of the interior of South Africa. However, between 1785 and 1791, the French went deep into the northern islands of Japan. Between 1768 and 1771, the British also discovered the Hawaiian Islands, Australia, and reached the Southern Ocean. In the 19th century, the main development was towards the interior of Asia and Africa. On the American side, Canada and the United States gradually expanded to the Pacific coast, and on the Australian side, the British gradually discovered the entire continent. In Africa, between 1861 and 1877, the British explored the sources of the Nile; between 1871 and 1885, Americans and Italians discovered the Congo Basin; and between 1861 and 1879, the British explored the situation in southern Africa and its major lakes. In Asia, the French began to invade Annam, the British went deep into India, and all Europeans concentrated their efforts on penetrating China to the interior. The sea route from north to west between America and Europe was successfully tested by Norwegians in 1906, and the sea route from north to east between Europe and Asia was also discovered by Norwegians between 1876 and 1879. The understanding of the Arctic is the result of exploration by the British, Americans, and Norwegians, especially the discoveries of the Norwegians between 1893 and 1896, and the Americans reaching the Arctic Circle in 1909, which are the most important. As for the Antarctic, the discovery of it was only in the 20th century. The most important were the British expeditions in 1902 and 1910, and the Norwegians reaching the South Pole in 1911. There are almost no secret places on the Earth's surface that have not been reached by humans. If there are any, they are only a few areas in the Arctic and Antarctic Circles, and only the highest peaks of the Pamir Plateau. However, last year and the year before, Soviet expeditions also made new record discoveries in the Arctic, and American expeditions discovered new land in the Antarctic. There are many explorers who are continuing to work hard there, regardless of the sacrifice of their lives! With the development of modern production technology, those secret areas are also nowhere to hide, with the most advanced icebreakers and airplanes attacking from both land and sea. Almost every point of the entire area of ​​the Earth has actually been captured in the eyes of humans. The ability of humans to conquer nature is truly great!

Weekly Literary Society

How to Write Short Stories

— Zhou Ge

While the essence of a short story doesn't fundamentally differ from that of a novel or novella, it does possess certain distinct characteristics. Without these specific traits, it couldn't be considered an independent form of fiction, nor could it be called a short story. Hamilton, in his "Short Story Law," defined a short story in this way: "The purpose of a short story is to evoke a unique narrative emotion with the greatest economy and the most compelling force." In his view, the so-called "narrative emotion" contains three elements: "action, characters, and setting." Although this definition superficially and partially states the characteristics of a short story, it is too abstract and technical to give us a clear concept of what a short story truly is. Frankly speaking, a simple definition cannot encompass everything about a short story because it is a branch of literature and a form of fiction. Besides possessing the general characteristics of literature and fiction, it has its own particular qualities.

However, what we urgently need to tell our readers here are the characteristics of a short story and the rules for writing one. What the essence of literature is and what the definition of fiction is don't seem to be the issues we should address here. Therefore, we don't want to start with literature and fiction and then talk about short stories, nor do we want to mechanically define a short story and then tell everyone how to write one. What we want to do is explain the characteristics of a short story and how to write one. This, hopefully, will be of some benefit to readers who want to or are beginning to learn how to write short stories.

First, there's the issue of subject matter. The subject matter that short stories adopt is, of course, like that of novels, social phenomena and stories of life. However, because short stories have a limited number of words, they cannot take large and complex stories as their subject. What they depict are certain corners of social phenomena! Small fragments of life. Complex subject matter like that adopted by Balzac in "The Human Comedy," Flaubert in "Madame Bovary," Zola in "The Rougon-Macquart series," Tolstoy in "War and Peace," and our own "Dream of the Red Chamber" and "Water Margin," etc., is absolutely unsuitable for short stories. Writers who are good at writing short stories take simple stories as their subject and describe life in a very concise yet detailed way.

However, while the subject matter of a good short story is a small fragment of life, this small fragment is a major life phenomenon existing in its era and society. Great short story writers have sharp eyes. They can see various important life phenomena in their era and society and can find stories and characters representative of those life phenomena to use as subject matter, and then vividly depict them. Therefore, the works they write can resonate with the majority of people and have great value. For example, the subject matter of Lu Xun's "The True Story of Ah Q" is a major social phenomenon in Chinese society during the Xinhai Revolution and the May Fourth Movement. The so-called "Ah Q-esque" life was the life of ordinary, muddle-headed, and sometimes self-important peasants in China at that time. Lu Xun seized this important social phenomenon of the era, taking Ah Q's life as the center, and vividly depicted it, so he achieved great success. Of course, the success of Lu Xun's "The True Story of Ah Q" is mainly due to his anti-feudal ideology and his sharp, satirical style, but the subject matter he adopted and his ideology and descriptive methods are greatly related.

From this, it seems that if you want to write a short story, you must first pay attention to the main social phenomena and use stories that represent these social phenomena as subject matter to start your creation. For example, in China at present, the main social phenomena are: rural bankruptcy, the decline of industry and commerce, unemployment and lack of education, the poverty of general life, and the resulting suicides and murders, as well as the "Rudinization" and "Hamletization" of most intellectuals, etc. If you want to write short stories, you must take a small but important fragment of these phenomena as subject matter and take a small fragment of the important real stories existing in these phenomena to construct your story. In this way, what you write will be noticed by everyone and will not be regarded as fabricating rumors or "playing at the extreme" for no reason.

Secondly, there is the issue of your thoughts. You know, literature loves truth. If you want to write a good short

Amateur Studies

From Elementary to Intermediate

— Ms. Liang

Dear Brother: Every time I pick up my pen to write to you, I feel an indescribable excitement.

I completely agree with the criticisms in your last letter. You said that reading too diffusely is the same as not reading at all. Indeed, I made this mistake in the past, and now I am willing to follow the reading plan you devised for me and proceed step by step.

With your help and that of other friends, I feel that I have made a lot of progress in the past six months. I remember when we parted for the last time, you said, "If you can't grasp life, you'll be crushed by it." I didn't understand its meaning at the time, but now I completely understand it! I want to be someone who grasps life. I want to fight. Brother, you watch.

You advised me to spend the time I used to spend reading miscellaneous books learning "Esperanto," and I did as you said. I attend the morning class of the Esperanto Association, which has been going on for more than a month. The location is in the alley across from the Carter Road Post Office, which is not too far from our factory. Recently, the factory extended working hours to eleven hours, and we have to start work at seven in the morning. My study time was resolved by getting the consent of the supervisor to move one hour in the morning to the evening. Although physically tired, I am very happy in spirit because I have already started to read some basic books and newspapers. Recently, the Esperanto Association has also held a summer class, and I have continued to join the intermediate level. Several friends saw how easy it was for me to learn Esperanto, and they also want to join the elementary research.

Will you still allow me to communicate in Esperanto in the future?

Mr. H, the teacher of our morning class, is an old classmate of yours. I have learned a lot of knowledge about various aspects from him. His language level is very good, and he is now starting to translate a collection of works of various small European ethnic groups from Esperanto, which will probably be published in September. In the future, he also plans to translate the Esperanto version of the famous Soviet film "Chapayev" into Chinese and has reserved me to help. I am of course very happy, so I am working hard to learn. You know that I have only been learning for more than forty days from the beginning until today, but I am already preparing to translate this large work of 200,000 words. Don't you think this is too ambitious?

Through Esperanto correspondence, I have met many honest friends at home and abroad who help and encourage me like you! My brother helps me and encourages me.

If you have the opportunity to come to Shanghai to see me, you must be happy for my gradual transformation into strength and courage, my brother!

Looking at the silent night outside the window and the twinkling stars, I seem to see your eyes burning with the fire of truth and hear the sound of your heart beating. The distance of space can never separate the resonance of our spirits, brother!

Waiting for your reply, I bless you and your career!

Sister, late night, July 11

Page 25

Story, you must not only take that important fragment as the subject matter, but also describe this fragment very realistically. But to describe this fragment of life very realistically, your subjective thoughts must be in line with the objective life phenomena—you can recognize the true essence of objective life phenomena. If your subjective thoughts are not in line with objective life phenomena, and you cannot recognize its reality, then you have no way to describe it very realistically, so the works you write will inevitably not be very successful. Poe said: "A skillful artist has constructed a tale. If wise, he has not fashioned his thoughts to accommodate his incidents; but having conceived, with deliberate care, a certain unique or single effect to be wrought out, he then invents such incidents -- he then combines such events as may best aid him in establishing this preconceived effect...." This really represents the words of people who fear the truth! If you write short stories according to this statement, then you don't care about objective facts, but only for your own private interests, you "invent incidents" based on your own subjectivity, even embellish reality, and create rumors. Is there still value in such works? If a person who is not afraid of objective reality, his own needs and thoughts are in line with the objective reality and needs, then he will not "invent incidents" or "accommodate facts." Under his understanding, the subject matter he adopts, the facts and thoughts he expresses, must be consistent with objective reality. Therefore, if you want to recognize objective reality and describe objective life phenomena very realistically, you must not be afraid of the truth, bravely approach objective reality, and stand in front of those who are not afraid of objective reality. If you work hard to write your short stories in this way, you will definitely make progress day by day.

Finally, there is the matter of descriptive methods. Because short stories have a limited number of words and limited subject matter, they must be written particularly concisely, without a single word of nonsense, and without using too many or too few words. All the overly long memories, extravagant narrations, excessive dialogues, and preachings in novels are things that should be avoided when writing short stories. Imagine, if Maupassant, when writing "The Necklace," wanted the woman who borrowed the necklace to go to a banquet to imagine all sorts of things after losing the necklace and compensating others with a huge amount of money, and to show all kinds of lives she went through, or even when she finally knew that the necklace she lost was fake, to create all kinds of pain and regret, or even to make a very long memory, then I dare say that "The Necklace" would definitely not be as good as it is, so amazing and admired. Those who are good at writing short stories pay great attention to the center of the thoughts or stories they express. They are good at tailoring, and anything that is not directly related to that center will be omitted by him. He just grasps that center and vividly describes it. Look, how rigorous is Lu Xun's "The True Story of Ah Q"? It can be said that there is not a single word that can be added or subtracted! This is a good short story. As for describing the story, whether to start from the end and trace back to the beginning? To start from the middle and unfold the whole story? Or to write from beginning to end? This can be up to you, it doesn't matter much. However, generally speaking, it is still good to write from beginning to end, especially when first learning to write short stories. At the same time, although the story described is very small, although it is a small fragment of life, it must still be linked to general phenomena when writing, to explain this small fragment from general phenomena, and to use this small fragment to prove general phenomena. For example, if you want to use the story of a young person who commits suicide due to unemployment or unrequited love as the subject matter, then you should not write from an individualistic point of view, but should describe it from a social point of view, to show the nature of the current society. Only in this way will others feel that you are telling the truth, and your work can move people, and thus have greater value.

Special Article

Overseas Chinese in the World (2)

— Zhong Minyi

At the same time, capitalism in Europe and the United States was still developing at that time. Phenomena such as economic recession and unemployment panic had not yet occurred. All places and industrial sectors needed a large amount of labor. The Chinese people had developed a "natural" spirit of hard work and endurance in their past commercial and agricultural social lives, which was suitable for the needs of European and American countries. Therefore, European and American countries often came to China to recruit Chinese laborers, and transported many mobile Chinese citizens overseas in batches. Furthermore, when capitalism in Europe and the United States was developing rapidly, there was an urgent need to open up markets and find natural resources: places such as Africa and Southeast Asia were areas with very abundant natural resources. Therefore, the forces of advanced European and American countries arrived in Africa and Southeast Asia one after another. However, Africa and Southeast Asia have always been relatively remote, and the population is very sparse. To develop their resources and prosper their markets requires not only a lot of labor, but also an increase in population. Thus, the hardworking Chinese people aroused great attention from the advanced European and American countries. In the past, there was a governor of the Dutch East Indies named Coen who left such an opinion to his successor when he stepped down: (To be continued)

Liu then surrendered, and the flesh and blood were reunited.

Movie News

Hunkuang Premieres at Central

Yue Ming's first sound film "Hunkuang", since its premiere at Jin Cheng, has been praised by all walks of life. The clear sound and audible dialogue have particularly surprised the audience. Foreign film merchants have been vying to purchase copies. Outlying areas such as Nanjing, Fujiang, Suzhou, Hangzhou, Hankou, etc. have premiered one after another, and business is booming. The film will premiere for the second time at the Central Grand Theater on Liu Malu on the 14th of this month. The play combines passionate love, righteousness, and chivalry into one. The content is unique. You, Zhu Guan, must be quick to see it.

Star Bimonthly will Publish a Welcome to Zhou Hu's Return to China Commemorative Issue

Zhou Hu, who traveled in Europe, has returned amidst the welcome of the masses. The enthusiastic scenes of the welcome, the graceful demeanor of Zhou Jianyun and his wife and Ms. Hu after the separation, and all the news and anecdotes during their trip are all things that everyone urgently needs to know. Under the enthusiastic request of readers, the Star Bimonthly will specially publish the "Welcome to Zhou Hu's Return to China Commemorative Special Issue" in Volume 2, Issue 1 (that is, the 7th issue in total), detailing all the experiences of Zhou Hu in various countries, various valuable photographs, and Zhou Jianyun and Ms. Hu Die's handwritten "European Travel Thoughts", three-color and two-color front and back covers, color-printed content is exquisite and rich, do you want to know the various situations when Zhou Hu returned to China? It is expected to break the current record in the publishing industry, please wait and see!

"Autumn Fan Bright Lamp" Continues to be Shown and Free Mink-Spotted Star Photos are Given Away

Lianhua Company's giant film "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp" was originally scheduled to be shown at the Jin Cheng Grand Theater until the day before yesterday. Later, because the weather has been hot in recent days, the box office has not declined slightly. The reason for this is nothing more than the popularity of the film and the excellent air-conditioning equipment of Jin Cheng. Therefore, the theater has specially decided to continue showing the film for several days, and at the same time, a photo of the new Lianhua star and the protagonist of the film, Mink Hua, will be attached to the ticket as a souvenir.
